commit 12e3420ab24860589bdf3d51b8d29edb9907d21b
Author: Andras Varga <andras@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Wed Sep 3 22:23:23 2025 +0200

    Aodv: add support for routing external addresses towards a gateway
    
    The AODV protocol had no support for routing to addresses in external
    IP networks. This commit implements a simple solution for the most
    basic use case: a single predefined, statically configured gateway.
    
    The gatewayAddress is a parameter of AODV (all nodes will know it).
    When a node encounters an external address, it adds a deafult (inactive)
    route to the gateway and starts route dicovery for the host defined by gatewayAddress.
    Once the route dicovered it forwards the queued packet according to that.
    
    - added suport to RoutingTable to properly display AODV maintained routes
    - fixed AODV to use the IP address of the interface configured for AODV
      instead of using the router ID (which might be different if multiple
      interfaces are present in the node - and also can be manually changed
      to any arbitrary ID)
    - added an additional configuration to examples/aodv to demonstrate the feature.
    
    Aodv: fixes for crash after default route was expunged

commit ba7e428f1208ed7da084a59d3120a16e18ca2c56
Author: Andras Varga <andras@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Mon Jan 5 08:29:30 2026 +0100

    Partially revert "InitStageRegistry.h: prepare macros for being used in another namespace"
    
    Restore previous definition of NUM_INIT_STAGES (that does not contain inet::).
    NUM_INIT_STAGES is used as inet::NUM_INIT_STAGES in Simu5G and potentially
    other derived projects as well. If we added "inet::" to the definition now,
    it would cause compile errors in Simu5G, requiring INET-version-dependent
    code in it to fix. We better leave the original definition.

commit b364ef3c98b48313fec9040e97a3f25173984274
Author: Levente Meszaros <levy@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Thu Dec 18 16:23:39 2025 +0100

    SettableClock: Refactored setClockTime to immediately execute/skip overdue clock events in clock time order.
    
    Previously, they were scheduled for the same simulation time, but it could terminate the simulation because
    the clock events and the corresponding clock/oscillator was left in inconsistent state. The clock was already
    set to the new clock time even though the overdue clock events were not yet executed.
    When the events were executed they set the clock time back.
    This also fixes #844.

commit b84ce385eb0d68f78048ea54ddbc8031b5c1c76c
Author: Zoltan Bojthe <zbojthe@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Tue Dec 9 17:15:02 2025 +0100

    applications/voipstream: Update deprecated FFmpeg API calls with version guards
    
    Modernized FFmpeg API usage in the voipstream application to support
    both legacy and current FFmpeg versions while eliminating deprecation
    warnings on newer versions.
    
    Changes:
    - Added version guards for avcodec_close() calls (deprecated since
      FFmpeg 3.1/libavcodec 58). The function is now only called for
      older FFmpeg versions, as avcodec_free_context() automatically
      closes the codec in newer versions.
    
    - Updated sample format retrieval in VoipStreamSender to handle the
      deprecated 'sample_fmts' field (deprecated since FFmpeg 6.1). The
      code now uses the legacy field for FFmpeg < 6.1 and the new
      avcodec_get_supported_config() API for FFmpeg >= 6.1.

commit d9965cb8933393eee7e6d4ed39ba2b292caaef5e
Author: Levente Meszaros <levy@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Thu Nov 20 12:13:29 2025 +0100

    Gptp: Refactored the complete protocol implementation.
    
    Replaced timestamp mechanism to capture the transmission/reception start time.
    Added state machines for peer delay measurement and time synchronization processes.
    Extracted the peer delay measurement process state for requester and responder roles into separate data structures.
    Extracted the time synchronization process state for sender and receiver roles into separate data structures.
    Added exponential mean for peer delay measurement.
    Changed bridge nodes to forward unmodified sync messages.
    Fixed peer delay measurement while a time synchronization is in progress by using the unsynchronized local clock.
    Added clock servo usage.
    Removed obsolete fields.

commit 0e5c15d07de93210ce104ff1eeb061906cf27871
Author: Levente Meszaros <levy@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Thu Dec 4 12:08:26 2025 +0100

    DriftingOscillatorBase: Removed default value from nominalTickLength.
    
    The 0 value no longer means simulation time precision, which didn't really
    make sense in the first place, because the change in tick length due to clock
    drift could not be represented accurately anyway.
    
    This change requires all simulations to explicitly set the clock nominalTickLength.
    Typically it would be set above simulation time precision with several orders of magnitude
    to make space for representing the current tick left accurately (due to clock drift).

commit 8d37699facb1f98ec9a455bb3736bc81c0d9d73c
Author: Zoltan Bojthe <zbojthe@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Tue Sep 16 14:33:04 2025 +0200

    BGP: Fix sessionEstablished flag not reset when transitioning to Idle state (#1050)
    
    When BGP FSM transitions from any state to Idle state (due to timeouts,
    connection failures, etc.), the sessionEstablished flag was not being
    reset to false. This caused BgpRouter::updateSendProcess to continue
    attempting to send update messages over closed TCP sockets, resulting
    in "TcpSocket::send(): socket not connected or connecting, state is CLOSED"
    errors.
    
    This issue was particularly visible in simulations with 10+ BGP routers
    where sessions would timeout (connectRetryTime = 120s) before completing
    information exchange.
    
    Fixed by ensuring sessionEstablished is set to false in all FSM state
    transition functions that call setState<Idle>().
    
    Fixes: BGP session timeout causing socket send errors

commit 47650f8b37862f7550d8a7176054821d3bfecddc
Author: Andras Varga <andras@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Tue Apr 15 13:00:37 2025 +0200

    checksum: overhaul, new CRC algorithms, verification
    
    - Rely on categorization on CRC Reveng https://reveng.sourceforge.io/crc-catalogue
      and online CRC calculator crccalc.com
    
    - Added new checksum algos: CRC32C, CRC16-IBM, CRC16-CCITT.
    
    - Added generic CRC implementations that take the same parameters as CRC RevEng
      uses (poly, init, refin, refout, etc.): generic_crc32(), generic_crc16(),
      generic_crc8().
    
    - Using the generici CRC functions above, and added "bitwise" implementations
      of CRC algos (e.g. crc32c_bitwise()). They are slow, and only used for
      verifying the table-based implementations
    
    - Added Checksum_1.test
    
    - Use uint8_t and size_t for arg types
    
    - Deleted unsupported CRC types CRC-8, CRC-64

commit 941b815411fc972d57db80acca13fc7091fa925a
Author: Andras Varga <andras@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Sat Apr 12 10:04:02 2025 +0200

    Consistently use the term "FCS" instead of "CRC" when talking about L2 frame checksums
    
    Before, the terminology was mixed (e.g. FCS in Ethernet, CRC in 802.11)
    
    crcMode parameters (notably, in Ieee80211Radio) were renamed to fcsMode.
    There is no longer a crcMode parameter anywhere, so **.crcMode assignments
    were removed from ini files.
    
    The CrcMode enum, parseCrcMode() etc were removed. Header fields use
    FcsMode instead.

commit 05a36c8a0e939e1041134066e4f667c52f89908c
Author: Andras Varga <andras@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Wed Apr 9 13:37:28 2025 +0200

    TCP/IP stack: rename "crc" fields to "checksum"
    
    TCP, UDP, SCTP, IPv4, IPv6, ICMP, IGMP, etc.
    
    These protocols actually use checksums (actual 16-bit one's complement
    sum of the headers), and not the Cyclic Redundancy Check algorithm.
    
    Non-compatible change: "crcMode" parameter renamed to "checksumMode"

commit 5bd6524398d8d8b6eb4a584e43871e78161e9a75
Author: Andras Varga <andras@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Mon Apr 7 14:34:17 2025 +0200

    checksum: Checksum inserters / Checkers revised
    
    Original motivation:
    - CrcHeaderInserter/CcrHeaderChecker computed TCP/IP checksum, not CRC
    - There were separate base classes for the Crc* and Fcs* modules,
      there should be a common one where the CRC algorithm is a parameter
    
    Changes:
    - Added ChecksumHeaderChecker/ChecksumHeaderInserter and ChecksumCheckerBase/
      ChecksumInserterBase modules, which accept a checksumType parameter
    
    - ChecksumMode moved into common/checksum
    
    - ChecksumType added into common/checksum
    
    - CrcHeaderInserter/CrcHeaderChecker: Became pure NED subclasses of ChecksumHeaderInserter/
      ChecksumHeaderChecker; and renamed to Crc32HeaderInserter, Crc32HeaderChecker
    
    - FcsHeaderInserter/FcsHeaderChecker: Became pure NED subclasses of ChecksumHeaderInserter/
      ChecksumHeaderChecker
    
    - EthernetFcsChecker, EthernetFcsInserter, EthernetFragmentFcsChecker,
      EthernetFragmentFcsInserter: ported to the new ChecksumCheckerBase and
      ChecksumInserterBase base classes
    
    - AccessoryProtocol: removed the CRC and FCS protocols, replaced with Checksum

commit 56c85f1acbadca69978f6835a9906dbc443bcf59
Author: Andras Varga <andras@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Thu Mar 13 09:08:38 2025 +0100

    Ieee80211AgentSta: partial fix for #1022: defaultSsid parameter enhanced.
    
    defaultSsid now accepts a list of SSIDs the node is allowed to connect to,
    and chooses the one with the best signal strength from them.
    
    If only one SSID is listed (such as in the default case, "SSID"), and
    there are multiple APs with that SSID, the agent will now choose the
    one with the strongest signal (instead of the first one as before).
    
    Refactoring: chooseBSS() now encapsulates all of BSS selection functionality.

Author: Andras Varga <andras@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Tue Nov 5 11:17:31 2024 +0100

    showcases and tutorials: adding "Try it Yourself" sections
    
    Script used:
    
    ```
    import os
    import re
    
    def modify_content(dirpath, content):
        # Parse INET version from the line '| INET version: ``4.2``'
        inet_version_match = re.search(r'\| INET version: ``([\d\.]+)``', content)
        if not inet_version_match:
            raise ValueError("INET version not found in content")
        inet_version = inet_version_match.group(1)
    
        # Extract subpath from dirpath
        subpath_match = re.search(r'./(.*?)/doc', dirpath)
        if not subpath_match:
            raise ValueError("Subpath not found in directory path")
        subpath = subpath_match.group(1)
    
        # Insert the required line before the line containing 'Discussion'
        insert_lines = f"""
    Try It Yourself
    ---------------
    
    If you already have INET and OMNeT++ installed, start the IDE by typing
    ``omnetpp``, import the INET project into the IDE, then navigate to the
    ``inet/showcases/{subpath}`` folder in the `Project Explorer`. There, you can view
    and edit the showcase files, run simulations, and analyze results.
    
    Otherwise, there is an easy way to install INET and OMNeT++ using `opp_env
    <https://omnetpp.org/opp_env>`__, and run the simulation interactively.
    Ensure that ``opp_env`` is installed on your system, then execute:
    
    .. code-block:: bash
    
        $ opp_env run inet-{inet_version} --init -w inet-workspace --install --chdir
           -c 'cd inet-{inet_version}/showcases/{subpath} && inet'
    
    This command creates an ``inet-workspace`` directory, installs the appropriate
    versions of INET and OMNeT++ within it, and launches the ``inet`` command in the
    showcase directory for interactive simulation.
    
    Alternatively, for a more hands-on experience, you can first set up the
    workspace and then open an interactive shell:
    
    .. code-block:: bash
    
        $ opp_env install --init -w inet-workspace inet-{inet_version}
        $ cd inet-workspace
        $ opp_env shell
    
    Inside the shell, start the IDE by typing ``omnetpp``, import the INET project,
    then start exploring.
    
    """.splitlines()
    
        modified_lines = []
        for line in content.splitlines():
            if line.strip() == 'Discussion':
                modified_lines.extend(insert_lines)
            modified_lines.append(line)
        return "\n".join(modified_lines)+"\n"
    
    def modify_files(root_directory):
        for dirpath, _, filenames in os.walk(root_directory):
            for filename in filenames:
                if filename == 'index.rst' and dirpath.endswith('doc'):
                    file_path = os.path.join(dirpath, filename)
                    print(f"Modifying: {file_path}")
    
                    # Read the original content
                    with open(file_path, 'r') as file:
                        content = file.read()
    
                    # Modify the content
                    modified_content = modify_content(dirpath, content)
    
                    # Write the modified content back to the file
                    with open(file_path, 'w') as file:
                        file.write(modified_content)
    
    if __name__ == "__main__":
        modify_files(".")
    ```

commit d73e3bce83ff9b7a76df2c182edbfca92c0cac19
Author: Chen Lijun <chenlijun1999@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Nov 29 17:03:58 2024 +0100

    NeighborListCache: don't build neighbor list during initialization (#983)
    
    Given n radios, neighbor list construction has O(n^2) complexity.
    If, during initialization, when each radio is added, the neighbor list
    is reconstructed, we end up having a simulation initialization with
    O(n^3) complexity.
    Sidenote: In one of our tests, without this patch, when running a WiFi
    simulation of 5000 nodes, it took ~40 minutes to just initialize the
    simulation.
    
    Co-authored-by: Levente Mészáros <levy@omnetpp.org>

commit 84ebff78ac5713966b9b81e8bceafb9d16202776
Author: Levente Meszaros <levy@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Fri Nov 15 14:56:35 2024 +0100

    all: Removed all ChangeLog files because they are no longer maintained.
    
    The decision to remove these files was made on a team meeting.
    
    With the recent advancements of AI technologies there are already better ways
    to extract more useful information from the git repository. Maintaining the
    ChangeLog files took a non-trivial amount of time; not important commits had
    to be filtered out, many commit messages were rephrased, more often than not
    commits affect somewhat unrelated folders, etc. Also, it was unclear who were
    the actual users of the ChangeLog files to begin with.

commit c39d80006b7940f8c9f6906b2f5b52167f8fd856
Author: Levente Mészáros <levy@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Wed Sep 13 16:17:54 2023 +0200

    EthernetCsmaMac: Extended TX_END transition in TRANSMITTING state with separate CRS and !CRS cases.
    
    The IFG period should not start if CRS is true. This is the case when PLCA is
    used and the transmission is delayed by the HOLD state in PLCA. The MAC started
    a new transmission while the PLCA was in DS_TRANSMIT state after an IFG period
    even though the CRS was set to true by the PLCA.

Date:   Wed Sep 6 17:07:42 2023 +0200

    EthernetPlca: Added syncing_timer to CS_Syncing state.
    
    The syncing timer separates the BEACON and the following COMMIT/DATA signals with a small amount of time.
    This is done for non-controller nodes to have a CRS OFF/ON spike in the SYNCING state to allow them to go into WAIT_TO.

commit 2d6ef74ef9d0e89e2db06447efc9c82e7aa8b89c

commit 7ee9cc46e11368b42f1da6912cd9d691b0946577
Author: Zoltan Bojthe <zbojthe@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Mon Sep 11 16:31:01 2023 +0200

    tcp: Tcp, TcpLwip: added autoRead=false mode and READ requests to allow TCP flow control
    
    Until now, all TCP sockets operated in "autoread" mode, i.e. all data
    that received in the TCP connection were immediately sent up to the app.
    
    This commit implements another mode, "explicit-read" mode. This mode means that
    the user must send an explicit read request, similar to a real-life socket
    read() call, and the TCP will respond either with already queued data, or
    if there is no queued data, with new data that arrives next on the
    connection. A limit for the number of bytes to be sent up ("buffer
    size") can be specified in the read request.
    
    TCP flow control is only effective in read mode. (An autoread TCP connection
    will always advertise the value set in the "advertisedWindow" parameter.)
    With READ mode, the advertised window will be decreased by newly arrived
    data unless READ requests make room in the buffer.
    
    Summary:
    - flow control only works in READ mode (autoread always advertizes full buffer size)
    - explicit-read mode can be turned on in TcpOpenCommand, by setting autoRead=false
      (autoRead is still the default, for backward compatibility)
    - a READ request is represented by TcpReadCommand, with numberOfBytes
      being an upper limit
    - after a READ request, issuing a new READ request is only allowed after
      the previous one has been fulfilled
    - related: sending up TCP_I_PEER_CLOSED indication after receiving a FIN
      is now delayed until all data have been read by the app
    
    TcpLwipConnection: autoread fixup

commit 2374e35c24214203045286b27f5d72e9f7b20b2c

commit da115df93db78cb7f5d0b50c2ce517265d550ad1
Author: Andras Varga <andras@omnetpp.org>
Date:   Tue Aug 29 15:04:09 2023 +0200

    GateScheduleCanvasVisualizer: fix runtime error on Windows
    
    The "displayTime=..." line produced simtime overflow error,
    because indexStart was bogus a huge positive integer.
    
    It was computed as:
    
    auto indexStart = (int)... * durations.size();
    
    which is signed * unsigned multiplication, whose result was signed on Linux,
    and unsigned on Windows.
    
    Workaround: factor out durations.size() as int numDurations, to eliminate
    mixed-sign multiplications in the code. Also, make indexStart / indexEnd
    explicit signed int.

commit d4025acfe3485772c4c81551dc83cdea06b40355
Author: Philipp Meyer <philipp.meyer@haw-hamburg.de>
Date:   Fri May 12 15:36:57 2023 +0200

    EligibilityTimeMeter: Fixed number of token statistic to not have negative values.
    
    Previously if the rate of incoming traffic was higher than the rate of outgoing
    traffic, the number of tokens statistic could be negative which doesn't really
    make sense. The number of tokens statistics is created by emitting values into
    the future such that a sawtooth pattern is created.
    The actual behavior of the ATS is not influenced by this change because the
    number of tokens is just a derived statistic for a virtual token bucket.
